text:
I used a good quality salsa, double-batch of homemade taco seasoning and double the cilantro. I made the end result into fajitas with sauteed red pepper, sweet onion and minced garlic. As always, I think the quality of your ingredients can make or break your recipe--I'm glad I doubled the spices and used a good salsa. We were quite hungry today so this fed us well with enough leftover for another meal, with the sauteed vegetables. I'll make this again.

text:
I do this all the time but if you get a salsa with a lot of flavor, you can omit the taco packet. It only adds extra sodium. Instead, use a jar of salsa, 2 minced garlic cloves and a diced onion. I also like to use two limes. :)
(and if you add the lime and fresh cilantro in the last hour of cooking you get MORE flavor)

They were simply the best I have ever had. text:
I prepared this for guests that are on low-calorie diets last evening, and it was a HUGE hit!  I served it with super low carb, high fiber tortillas, salsa and fat free sour cream, and it was YUMMY!  Definitely a keeper, and it makes a large amount.  A serving is a large portion, very flavorful and filling.  Even my picky son LOVED it and asked to have it again tomorrow!  I followed some of the suggestions other reviewers had, such as not using the full pack of taco seasoning because of the high sodium content.  I added rinced black beans, drained whole kernel corn, and I sliced up two medium onions and added it to the mixture.  I threw this together on my lunch break and it cooked on high for about 4 hours and the chicken just fell apart and was so moist and juicy.  I will make this over and over again...no doubt!

text:
I know this may sound crazy but this recipes make a fantastic easy spicy Indian chicken curry.  I used a jar Tostito's Chunky medium salsa,  2 x packs of dry taco mixes.  1/2 cup of fresh cilantro and the juice of two small limes.  I added all these ingredients together at the start like the recipe states, that in the last couple of hours I added 2 chopped onions and 1/2 small yellow pepper and 1/2 small green pepper and 4 small Jalapenos.  The taste was gorgeous, served with wild rice and Garlic naan breads.  I will be making this recipe again and again...

text:
I've been on a crock pot kick this week, and this is the best dish I've made in my slow cooker yet! My family was raving about this one. I'm a cilantro fan, so I added a full cup of the fresh herb. I wasn't sure what salsa to use, so I did 8oz. of Pace coupled with 8oz. of a Fresh Serrano Salsa I purchased at Trader Joes. Truthfully, I think you are safe using a canned Salsa like Pace because the Taco Seasoning becomes the dominant flavor in the salsa. I would not use dry cilantro, however...for me, the fresh cilantro made this dish!! Fantastic recipe that I'll be making over and over again. Super Easy to make, but your friends will think you are a Culinary Genius!!!

text:
This was a great recipe to start with, but I made some modifications:

Used a 24-ounce jar of salsa instead of 16. Use a good salsa, not Pace or anything like that. Omitted taco seasoning and instead seasoned chicken with garlic salt, pepper, cumin, oregano, paprika, crushed red pepper, and a teensy bit of cayenne pepper (if you're not into spicy you might want to omit the last two). Added 1/2 green bell pepper and 1/2 onion. Only used half a lime, set the other half aside. Before making the salsa mixture, I poured about 1/2 inch coating of *salsa only* on the bottom, just to wet it, then did up my chicken, then poured the finished salsa mixture on top. Once cooked I sprinkled on more cilantro and the juice from the remaining lime, and served with Spanish rice.

This turned out so juicy and good, all those seasonings soaked into that chicken and the chicken was so moist I didn't need a knife! Great recipe.

text:
This recipe is easy and delicious. For the people complaining that the chicken was 'dry', it doesn't matter how much liquid one uses to cook chicken breasts, if they're overcooked they'll be 'dry' i.e. have a 'mealy' texture, and timing for a better outcome can be tricky.
This is why I rarely buy breasts and use thighs where I can, which I used in this recipe. Now, to overcome the 'tricky' timing for a moist breast, I brine the breasts 24 hours ahead of time.  This takes some advance planning, but what a difference it makes, and the brine is simple; 1qt water, 1/2cup Kosher salt and 1/4 cup white sugar. Can adjust amount to fit needs, just keep the ratio the same. This method really makes a difference in the breast texture.  That said, they of course, can still be overcooked, but the timing is not as critical. Brining can be done for any recipe calling for chicken or pork. Hope this helps.

The amount of liquid in the slow cooker is only enough to create a thin layer on the bottom, with a ton of chicken on top, uncovered.  In addition, the cooking time is way off--I used 4 frozen chicken breasts (much less than the 3 lbs called for in the recipe) cooked on low and after 4 hours it was cooked completely through and could be shredded by a fork.  The recommended cooking time, combined with the lack of liquid, would have ruined the meat.  I added 3 cups of chicken broth, an extra lime, and more cilantro.  I cooked on low for 4 hours, then removed the chicken, shredded it with a fork, and put it back in for 30 more minutes.  When it was done I strained the chicken out of the liquid and put it on tortillas with cheese and sour cream as tacos, which was very good.  The crockpot dish itself looked like a soup before I strained it, however.

Absolutely one of my favorite recipes on this site! Super easy, very good and versatile. The only difference in mine is that instead of using a prepackaged taco seasoning, I make my own. It's truly a gem on this site, and something anyone can recreate.

text:
Decided to try this because I have a ton of cilantro in the garden.  I went with CookinBug's suggestion of making my own taco mix instead of using a pre-made, packaged mix.  They're mostly salt, so it becomes very expensive salt with a few cents worth of other ingredients.  I also made green salsa from the tomatilloes, jalapenos and cilantro in the garden instead of using bottled salsa.  I used more cilantro than called for and held it out until after the chicken was cooked.  I feel this brings through the fresh flavor of the cilantro.  The result was delicious, but it's definitely not for those cilantro haters out there (you know who you are!)

I'm usually a "no cilantro please" kind of person, but I took a chance with this recipe because I love using my slow cooker.  I'm super happy I did.  Along with some homemade tortillas and chili corn, this recipe was really good (also added avocado and sour cream).  The salsa didn't cover my chicken, so I added a can of chicken broth.  The chicken still came out a tad drier than most meat I cook in my slow cooker, so next time I would probably add a second jar of salsa to make it more tender (I cooked on low for 7.5 hours).  I'm also usually a 'don't eat leftovers' person (food just never tastes right reheated to me), but I'm currently enjoying the chicken for lunch - another bonus.  Would definitely recommend this recipe.  Maybe it's because I love salty foods, but I didn't notice this being overly salty at all - has just the right amount of salt and kick for me!

text:
Loved this recipe.  I get requests to share it from guests and love how I can do all the prep ahead of time and just let it cook through our busy afternoons.  

I made it with just a pound of chicken, 2/3 jar of salsa, 2 T cilantro, juice from 1 lime and half the taco seasoning.   It wasn't too spicy for my kids and the higher salsa to chicken ration made it moist, not dry.  It was delicious and plenty of food for four adults.  I have cooked it twice once on Low in the slow cooker and once on High for the shorter amount of time.  Both worked great and the chicken shredded beautifully.  I used a taco seasoning recipe from this site since I already had the spices in my kitchen.

 Added additional fresh cilantro, garlic powder and onion powder, salt,pepper 2 hours into cooking. I also made this on the stove on low heat for 3-4 hours and it was so tender and delicious. The flavor was amazing! Served it over white rice and  made tacos ( corn tortillas, cheese, salsa, guacamole, sour cream)the next day. This is a new family favorite!

text:
Absolutely amazing! I'm embarrassed to admit it, but it was my first time ever cooking with fresh Cilantro. This was wonderful! I will be using Cilantro more often, WOW what flavor it truly adds! I shred the chicken after it was cooked for 6 hours on low (shredded using a hand blender on the lowest speed - try it, this shredding trick really does work). I then put it back in the crock pot for another half hour to finish marrying together. We used the chicken mixture in tortillas with a small amount of sour cream & cheese, and any preferred sauce. We did find that a mexican flavored rice goes much better with this chicken recipe, instead of spanish rice which is what we did the first time. Also you could put rice inside the tortillas with the chicken mixture as well, and that is yummy to! It was a very nice change of pace for us! We love it so much, that now we're making a large batch of this to also use for a couple of different mexican style dishes to use in for the week to save time! Love, love, love it!!

text:
I had a freezer-burned bag of chicken thigh strips that I knew could only be saved by a slow cooker recipe.  Not only was this one edible, it was very good...even my picky kids ate it!  I literally just threw the frozen mass of chicken in my slow cooker with the other ingredients, cooked on high and stirred until it thawed, then set it on low until done.  Easy, and I have enough left over for another meal (enchiladas this time).  I doubled the cilantro and lime, and used an Ortega 40% less sodium taco seasoning packet.  I can see where using a regular packet would be too salty, so I will definitely use the reduced sodium packet again.  Next time I will use a fresh salsa or pico de gallo, which I think will enhance the taste, and I can't wait to make it again with fresh chicken.  But if you have a chunk of freezer-burned chicken, don't toss it, make this recipe.

text:
I was trying to find something new for low-calorie lunches for work and this fit the bill perfectly! After reading the reviews of how salty the recipe can get with a packet of taco seasoning (and trying to keep to a low sodium diet), I omitted the packet and used McCormicks Salt-Free Southwest Seasoning. I halved the recipe and only used about 2 Tbls. of salsa (since that is loaded with sodium), and threw in a whole can of low sodium petite diced tomatoes. I also had some red onion and added about 1/4 cup of those. Those were the only changes I made and it was so delicious. Served on a whole wheat tortilla with light sour cream and low-fat cheddar cheese made for yummy lunches that were the talk of the office!

This was SO GOOD!!! I followed the ingredients and amounts exactly plus added a can of drained Mexi corn shortly before serving (just to heat the corn through). I threw this together over lunch and put it on low for about six hours - it was PERFECT when I got home from work! The chicken just fell apart and shredded perfectly. I served this with a Cilantro Lime Rice recipe I found on here - when I make this again I'll probably serve with just regular rice (the Cilantro Lime Rice was delicious but maybe too much lime and cilantro between that and the chicken) or even in tortillas/tacos. Regardless, this will definitely be a regular for me. It was almost better as leftovers too! Overall just a great recipe - very few ingredients (cheap!), little prep time (easy!), and DELICIOUS!!!

OMG. I love this recipe. I have made this about a dozen times. It is great as it but I have been making modifications lately and like it even more! I have made this recipe a few times now, and it's probably the simplest recipe I have EVER made. The best part of course is that it tastes great. I think I eat it every meal until it's gone. I loved this recipe. The only thing I changed was to double the taco seasoning. 

I read where someone thought the 6 hours on low had burned the salsa and that the sauce was too runny, however, I did not have this problem. 

The salsa cooked perfectly on 6 hours at low setting and the sauce wasn't soupy at all once I shredded the chicken. 

I added a can of black beans at the end and served it over white rice. This is a keeper and I will definitely be making it again.

Wow!!  Very tasty and easy!!  I used taco seasoning I recipe from this site. I made recipe as is with the exception of  taking the advice of others, I added a 12 oz. bag of sweet corn niblets and 15 oz can of black beans.  I put them in when there was 1 1/2 hours until it was done as I was leaving for evening church.  Mine turned out more like a soup as the salsa I used was from a bulk store in a large container and had more liquid in it.  My husband who is a soup lover ate it that way.  I saute'd red and green pepper slices and sweet yellow onion and then used a slotted spoon to drain the chicken mixture and had mine wrapped in a tortilla with cheese and sour cream, YUM!!!  We are making nachos with the left overs today and I am sure there will be enough for my husband to have a couple bowls of soup!  Makes a lot!!  Thanks for sharing a great tasting and EASY recipe.  I made a jar of the taco seasoning I by Bill Echols  (I calculated for 64 servings) from this recipe and then just scoop out what a need for recipes calling for taco seasoning.

I made this last night and it was fantastic! A couple of changes, though. Instead of regular taco seasoning I used a small jar of Penzey's Chili 9000, which has no sodium, but is very spicy.  I added more cilantro (we like cilantro), and after squeezing the lime juice into the pot, I added the peel to the pot.  This added to the lime flavor. I also used chicken thighs instead of breasts. My husband, who never raves, raved. This will go into the family cookbook, for sure!

text:
I decided to make this recipe and then read the negative reviews the morning I was going to make this. So I made a few alterations but I'm not sure it made that much of a difference. I can say that the recipe came out very good and I would definitely make it again. I might even try it without my alterations to see how the original recipe was.
My changes were: 
1: I added about 1/2 cup of water to the salsa jar to rinse it out and put it into the crockpot.
2: I diced up and added 1 small onion and 2 cloves of garlic.
3: I sprinkled about 1/2 tablespoon each of  cumin and chili powder on top of the chicken after coating it with the salsa mixture. 
4: Mix it up and flip the chicken 1/2 way through cooking time.

text:
My family absolutely loved this recipe. We had it for dinner and it's a new favorite. I used chunky medium salsa added 2 cups of water for more juice, 1 package of fiesta chicken taco mix by McCormick, 5 tablespoons fresh cilantro, and 2 full  Fresh squeezed limes juice. Plus 1/2 can of cento black beans.  After stirring everything together i added 3 skinless boneless chicken breasts. Cooked in my crockpot on high for 4 hour's. It came out so flavorful, juicy, moist chicken, it was out of this world and very simple to make. I heated up soft tacos, placed lettuce down first with more fresh cilantro, then added the chicken & juices from the crockpot, some shredded cheese and a dollop of sour cream. This is a new favorite for our family.

text:
I've been making a modified version of this dish for several years.  The recipe as written is a good base but it lacks substance to be a standalone meal which is typically my goal when using the crock pot.  I add extra cilantro & lime, a can of black beans (drained and rinsed), a can of corn (drained) or half bag of frozen corn, and use fresh salsa (Jack's brand is my fave)  vs canned.  We typically serve on flour tortillas with sour cream and shredded cheese or with tortilla chips as a party appetizer.  This was a perfect dish for busy evenings when everyone was eating at different times. Also freezes well.

It ended up being a 5 star recipe!

text:
Dry brined the chicken, then seared it before adding to the crockpot. Low for 9 hours, easily forkable and not dry.

Goya salsa pico de gallo was a great choice for the salsa. Thick and chunky enough to withstand the long cooking and retain some texture.

Taco seasoning was just thrown in spices, mostly typical, but did add 2 bayleaves and a touch of brown sugar.

Frozen corn and can of black beans (strained) just plopped in also. Terrific additions.

I added a bit of water (maybe 1/2 cup) to make sure everything was covered, but it was a bit soupy in the end, so I'd probably omit it next time, as the water level rose during cooking.

Overall I made a few additions, but flavor was good enough to not need anything. That plus the ease, health, and relative inexpense gives this a 5.

text:
Well, I hate reviewing a recipe when I don't make it exactly as written but I just had to share what I did as it turned out great!  Not by choice, but only because I didn't have the exact ingredients on hand.  First, there are only two of us so I only used two boneless skinless chicken breast halves.  Placed them in an ungreased crockpot.  Put a little salt and pepper on top.  In a separate bowl, I combined 1/2 jar of strained  Frontera Tomatillo Salsa (Medium), juice of 1/2 lime, 3 tablespoons chopped fresh cilantro then about 1 tablespoon of Chef Merito Red Fajitas Seasoning.  Note that straining the salsa is important as recommended by another reviewer.  The end result wasn't too soupy but the meat was still very very moist.  After combining these ingredients just pour over and spread it around the top of the chicken breasts.  Cover and cook on  low for about 4 hours.  Shred and serve with your favorite condiments.  We had it with flour tortillas, sour cream, fresh cilantro, lettuce, tomatoes and jack cheese.  Yummmmmmy!  Thanks so much for this wonderful recipe!  I will try it the original way next time!! :)

After reading the reviews I added 1 chopped onion, 1 diced jalapeno, 1 jar salsa and 1 pkg. Fernandez taco sauce mix, 3 chicken breasts and a tablespoon of vegetable oil with the juice of 2 limes and extra cilantro.    Cooked on low 5 hours. text:
This has become one of my wife's most requested meals (that I cook). She doesn't like hot spice at all.  I've used an organic mild taco seasoning and mild salsa.  I've also added diced tomatoes to the recipe a couple of times as well, to turn down the heat when using warmer salsas or to extend cooking time if I want to cook it longer.  

Next step is to do away with any store bought taco seasoning and make my own using some of the recipes listed here.  

I've also used different salsas.  No Pace Picante (grin).  I've mainly used local made, artisan type salsas, which help to give it a little more variety.  I use a lime, cabbage, and carrot taco slaw (from by: mixingmedias here on Allrecipes) that is a great topper.  Then normally add cheese, sour cream or Greek yogurt, sliced black olives, chopped onion, and fresh cilantro.  

Very easy recipe. I increased ingredients and made it as a self serve taco bar one night for four couples.

text:
I'm not thrilled with this recipe.  It is rather bland.  After four hours in the slow cooker it was very tender and easy to shred, but just nothing special to taste.  I shredded it and then left it in the cooker for another 30 minutes after adding A LOT of additional spices: cumin, chili powder, onion and garlic powder, salt and pepper.  Then I also added juice from another lime and finally about another tablespoon of cilantro.  It was just ok even after that.  I served it in a bowl with all the standard taco toppings; avocado, cheese, lettuce, tomato, salsa verde. For leftovers tonight I'll serve it over rice with same taco toppings and see if it got better over night in the fridge.  This makes a lot.

This recipe was a last minute thing and it turned out so awesome.  I cooked it on low for 5 hours and i had a few minor changes.  FIrst , i used a little less than a full taco seasoning packet ( Old El Paso's Hot and Spicy)  to keep the heat under control. I didnt have any cilantro on hand but can only imagine how it would blow the dish over the top!  I also added a few TB's of chopped garlic.  Finally i didnt have a full jar of salsa but it still worked out great.  The dish was done after cooking on low for 5 hours and had a lot of liquid in the pot but after shredding the chicken it was just a little wet.  My family loved it and this is definitely a keeper in my  Tuesday night Taco/Mexican rotation.

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
It came out really good!  I did make quite a bit of changes.  First, I don't eat salsa in a jar.  I grew up with fresh salsa made with fresh roasted chiles   I made my own salsa and added the cilantro to it.  I used ~4 - 6oz of fresh roasted green chiles and jalapenos, 15oz can of tomatoes and minced garlic, onion powder and salt to taste.  Blended in blender to desired consistency then added to slow cooker.
Then I added 5 0z of canned tomatoes in blender, with 3 tablespoons of smashed chipotle peppers in adobo sauce and lime juice for one lime with 3.25 tablespoons home mixed Mexican seasoning (I avoid packaged taco seasoning due to all the sodium and preservatives) with 1.5 teaspoon of corn starch (to thicken sauce while cooking) and blended well.   Added mixture to slow cooker.
Cooked in slow cooker for 5 hours and when done shredded the meat and served with home made corn tortillas, lettuce, tomatoe, and chipotle Monterey jack cheese.  I added some of the extra sauce to the top of the tacos and it was EXCELLENT!.  Great new spin on tacos I never thought of.  Thanx for the idea.

text:
I made this yesterday and followed the suggestion of another to make my own taco seasoning (found on this site) and everything else I followed. I do agree that it was very salty which is weird coming from me because I normally enjoy to much salt! I should have left it out of the taco seasoning. Other then that it was really easy and you can def work at it and make it to your liking. It's a good base recipe to tweak as you go. The 2nd night we made enchiladas with the chicken and omg it was so much better the 2nd night. It was restaurant quality! We even have enough for tomorrow night and we will make fajitas. It makes a ton! Next time I will use 3 or 4 breast. 3lbs came to 6 breasts. Unless you freeze it or have a big family i would scale back on just the chicken portion. Oh and I used Pace salsa because that's all I had and it was still good. I'm not sure a better brand would really make a big difference but to each his own. Enjoy!!

text:
There are only 2 of us, so half the chicken, salsa, and low sodium taco seasoning.  I used 4+ tbsp. of cilantro and a whole small lime. It was plenty of wet contents for the amount of chicken.  I added 3 tbsp. of chopped onion and half a drained can of corn (no salt added).  The corn added a lot of flavor.  Cooked it on low in a crock pot for 2 hours and that was plenty then shredded it.  We ate it in whole wheat tortillas and/or baked Tostitos.  Low calorie meal but watch the sodium!  Whoever said omitting taco seasoning was a good idea was very wrong.  It adds most of the flavor to the meat itself.
